<script>
    window.addEventListener('load', function () {
        const announcementBar = document.getElementById('announcement-bar');
        const messages = [
            document.getElementById('message1'),
            document.getElementById('message2'),
            document.getElementById('message3'),
 document.getElementById('message4'),
        ];

        // Retrieve the last shown message index from localStorage
        let currentIndex = parseInt(localStorage.getItem('currentMessageIndex') || '0', 10);

        // Hide all messages initially
        messages.forEach((message) => {
            message.style.display = 'none';
        });

        // Show the current message
        messages[currentIndex].style.display = 'flex';

        // Show the announcement bar
        setTimeout(() => {
            announcementBar.style.display = 'flex';
            document.body.classList.add('with-announcement');
        }, 10000); // 10-second delay

        // Update the index for the next page load
        currentIndex = (currentIndex + 1) % messages.length;
        localStorage.setItem('currentMessageIndex', currentIndex);

        // Close button functionality
        document.getElementById('close-announcement').addEventListener('click', function () {
            announcementBar.style.display = 'none';
            document.body.classList.remove('with-announcement');
        });
    });
</script>

{"@context":"https:\/\/schema.org\/","@type":"NewsArticle","@id":"https:\/\/cyble.com\/blog\/hunters-become-the-hunted\/#newsarticle","url":"https:\/\/cyble.com\/blog\/hunters-become-the-hunted\/","headline":"Cyble - Clipper Malware disguised as AvD Crypto Stealer","mainEntityOfPage":"https:\/\/cyble.com\/blog\/hunters-become-the-hunted\/","datePublished":"2022-03-22T12:28:50-04:00","dateModified":"2025-05-20T05:02:35-04:00","description":"Cyble Research Labs analyzes a Clipper malware variant disguised as an AvD Crypto-stealer, potentially targeting other Threat Actors.","articleSection":"Phishing","articleBody":"Information stealing malware is on the rise. Cyble Research Labs recently discovered a new malware dubbed \u201cAvD crypto stealer\u201d on a cybercrime forum. Upon further investigation, however, we observed that this does not function as a Crypto Stealer. This is, in fact, a disguised variant of well-known Clipper malware that can read and edit any text copied by the victim i.e. crypto wallet information.    The TA is providing one month of free access to entice more individuals to use it. Anyone can become a victim of this malware \u2013 though the primary target appears to be other TAs.    The Threat Actor (TA) claims that the stealer supports six cryptocurrency chains, including Ethereum, Binance Smart Chain, Fantom, Polygon, Avalanche, and Arbitrum.    The TA targets victims by changing the crypto addresses present in the clipboard. As for crypto transactions, individuals typically copy the crypto addresses, and the malware takes advantage of this by replacing the copied crypto wallet address with the one specified by TA.    If the victim does not validate the copied and the pasted values, then the transaction might end up in the account specified by TA. This clipper malware can also identify the crypto addresses present amongst multiple strings, expanding this malware\u2019s capabilities.    Figure 1: Post shared on a cybercrime forum    Technical Analysis    The execution of malware starts from an installation file, which is Self-Extracting. Self-extracting archives, also known as SFX files, are Windows executable files that, upon execution, extract the compressed content. Figure 2 showcases the installation wizard.    Figure 2: Installation Wizard    The installation file drops the files shown in Figure 3 and executes the payload named \u2018Payload.exe.\u2019 The dropped files also contain manuals for using the builder and the binaries.    Figure 3: Extracted files    The payload file (SHA256:b6135c446093a19544dbb36018adb7139aa810a3f3eaa45663dc54448fe30e39) is a .NET based binary. Figure 4 shows the payload details.    Figure 4: File information    Figure 5 shows the process flow for the clipper malware. The malware extracts the data from the clipboard and then uses a regular expression to find the crypto addresses. If there\u2019s a match, the malware replaces the address with one specified by TA.    Figure 5: Clipper malware process flow    Clipper malware has the following class names:    Program:    This class contains the main function which executes the clipper functionalities. Upon execution, the main program creates a random mutex named \u201cXWj1iK27ngY68XUB\u201d to ensure that only one instance of the malware process runs at any given time. If it fails to create a mutex, the malware terminates its execution.    Figure 6: Main function    After creating the mutex, the malware copies itself into the startup location to establish its persistence and executes ClipboardNotification.NotificationForm() function. Through this, the malware monitors the user\u2019s clipboard activity, identifies crypto address, and replaces it with the attacker\u2019s address details.&nbsp;    Clipboard Notification:    &nbsp;This class monitors the user\u2019s clipboard activity and notify when the user copies something into the clipboard.    Addresses:    This class contains the config details, including crypto addresses, mutex name, and the targeted cryptocurrencies, as shown in Figure 7. The clipper targets Bitcoin (BTC), Ethereum, and Monero (XMR) crypto addresses.    Figure 7: Addresses class    Clipboard:    The class contains two function names, GetText() and SetText().    These functions get the clipboard text from the user. If there is a crypto wallet in the copied text, these functions will then set it to the attacker\u2019s wallet address by replacing the copied user\u2019s wallet address. Clipboard is also responsible for sending the data for logging purposes to the URL present in the Addresses class.    Figure 8: Clipboard class    PatternRegex:    This class contains the regex pattern to identify the crypto addresses copied to the clipboard.    Figure 9: Pattern Regex    On further investigation into one of the hardcoded crypto addresses in the payload, we found the following transaction details, as shown below.    Figure 10: Transaction details        Conclusion:    Threat Actors continue to exploit the human element for executing their attacks, as they see it as a vulnerability - this malware works on a similar attack vector. However, we can reduce the impact of this malware by being more cautious while making crypto transactions.    There are multiple possibilities in which this attack can escalate. In one of the scenarios, the malware creator can target other TA\u2019s who use the builder for customizing the crypto stealer and their victims. This clipper can do financial theft at a great level, so it becomes necessary to take preventive measures.    Our Recommendations:&nbsp;     Avoid downloading pirated software from warez\/torrent websites. The \u201cHack Tool\u201d present on sites such as YouTube, torrent sites, etc., primarily contains such malware.\u00a0    Use a reputed anti-virus and internet security software package on your connected devices, including PC, laptop, and mobile.\u00a0    Refrain from opening untrusted links and email attachments without first verifying their authenticity.\u00a0\u00a0    In the case of businesses, educate employees in terms of protecting themselves from threats like phishing\u2019s\/untrusted URLs.\u00a0    Monitor the beacon on the network level to block data exfiltration by malware or TAs.\u00a0     MITRE ATT&amp;CK\u00ae Techniques\u202f&nbsp;    Tactic&nbsp;Technique ID&nbsp;Technique Name&nbsp;Initial Access&nbsp;T1566&nbsp;Phishing&nbsp;Execution\u202f&nbsp;T1204&nbsp;User Execution&nbsp;PersistenceT1547Boot or Logon AutoStart ExecutionCollection&nbsp;T1115Clipboard DataExfiltrationT1567Exfiltration Over Web Service    Indicators of Compromise (IoCs):    IndicatorsIndicator typeDescription012fca9cf0ac3e9a1c2c1499dfdb4eaf 47480d9b4df34ea1826cd2fafc05230eb195c0c2 <script src="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/jquery/3.6.0/jquery.min.js?ver<%=DateTime.Now.Ticks.ToString()%>" type="text/javascript"></script>
  
  
  
  <script src="https://unpkg.co/gsap@3/dist/gsap.min.js?ver<%=DateTime.Now.Ticks.ToString()%>" type="text/javascript"></script>
  
  
  
  <script src="https://unpkg.com/gsap@3/dist/Draggable.min.js?ver<%=DateTime.Now.Ticks.ToString()%>" type="text/javascript"></script>
  
  
  <script>
  document.addEventListener("DOMContentLoaded", function() {
      let loops = gsap.utils.toArray('.text-single').map((line, i) => {
          const links = line.querySelectorAll(".js-text"),
              tl = horizontalLoop(links, {
                  repeat: -1,
                  speed: 1 + i * 0.5,
                  draggable: true,
                  reversed: false,
                  paddingRight: parseFloat(gsap.getProperty(links[0], "marginRight", "px"))
              });
          links.forEach(link => {
              link.addEventListener("mouseenter", () => gsap.to(tl, {timeScale: 0, overwrite: true}));
              link.addEventListener("mouseleave", () => gsap.to(tl, {timeScale: i ? -1 : 1, overwrite: true}));
          });
      });
  
      let currentScroll = 0;
      let scrollDirection = 1;
  
      window.addEventListener("scroll", () => {
          let direction = (window.pageYOffset > currentScroll) ? 1 : -1;
          if (direction !== scrollDirection) {
              loops.forEach(tl => gsap.to(tl, {timeScale: direction, overwrite: true}));
              scrollDirection = direction;
          }
          currentScroll = window.pageYOffset;
      });
  
    function horizontalLoop(items, config) {
      items = gsap.utils.toArray(items);
      config = config || {};
      let tl = gsap.timeline({repeat: config.repeat, paused: config.paused, defaults: {ease: "none"}, onReverseComplete: () => tl.totalTime(tl.rawTime() + tl.duration() * 100)}),
          length = items.length,
          startX = items[0].offsetLeft,
          times = [],
          widths = [],
          xPercents = [],
          curIndex = 0,
          pixelsPerSecond = (config.speed || 1) * 100,
          snap = config.snap === false ? v => v : gsap.utils.snap(config.snap || 1), // some browsers shift by a pixel to accommodate flex layouts, so for example if width is 20% the first element's width might be 242px, and the next 243px, alternating back and forth. So we snap to 5 percentage points to make things look more natural
          populateWidths = () => items.forEach((el, i) => {
        widths[i] = parseFloat(gsap.getProperty(el, "width", "px"));
        xPercents[i] = snap(parseFloat(gsap.getProperty(el, "x", "px")) / widths[i] * 100 + gsap.getProperty(el, "xPercent"));
      }),
      getTotalWidth = () => items[length-1].offsetLeft + xPercents[length-1] / 100 * widths[length-1] - startX + items[length-1].offsetWidth * gsap.getProperty(items[length-1], "scaleX") + (parseFloat(config.paddingRight) || 0),
        totalWidth, curX, distanceToStart, distanceToLoop, item, i;
      populateWidths();
    gsap.set(items, { // convert "x" to "xPercent" to make things responsive, and populate the widths/xPercents Arrays to make lookups faster.
          xPercent: i => xPercents[i]
      });
      gsap.set(items, {x: 0});
      totalWidth = getTotalWidth();
      for (i = 0; i < length; i++) {
          item = items[i];
          curX = xPercents[i] / 100 * widths[i];
          distanceToStart = item.offsetLeft + curX - startX;
          distanceToLoop = distanceToStart + widths[i] * gsap.getProperty(item, "scaleX");
          tl.to(item, {xPercent: snap((curX - distanceToLoop) / widths[i] * 100), duration: distanceToLoop / pixelsPerSecond}, 0)
            .fromTo(item, {xPercent: snap((curX - distanceToLoop + totalWidth) / widths[i] * 100)}, {xPercent: xPercents[i], duration: (curX - distanceToLoop + totalWidth - curX) / pixelsPerSecond, immediateRender: false}, distanceToLoop / pixelsPerSecond)
            .add("label" + i, distanceToStart / pixelsPerSecond);
          times[i] = distanceToStart / pixelsPerSecond;
      }
      function toIndex(index, vars) {
          vars = vars || {};
          (Math.abs(index - curIndex) > length / 2) && (index += index > curIndex ? -length : length); // always go in the shortest direction
          let newIndex = gsap.utils.wrap(0, length, index),
              time = times[newIndex];
          if (time > tl.time() !== index > curIndex) { // if we're wrapping the timeline's playhead, make the proper adjustments
              vars.modifiers = {time: gsap.utils.wrap(0, tl.duration())};
              time += tl.duration() * (index > curIndex ? 1 : -1);
          }
          curIndex = newIndex;
          vars.overwrite = true;
          return tl.tweenTo(time, vars);
      }
      tl.next = vars => toIndex(curIndex+1, vars);
      tl.previous = vars => toIndex(curIndex-1, vars);
      tl.current = () => curIndex;
      tl.toIndex = (index, vars) => toIndex(index, vars);
    tl.updateIndex = () => curIndex = Math.round(tl.progress() * (items.length - 1));
      tl.times = times;
    tl.progress(1, true).progress(0, true); // pre-render for performance
    if (config.reversed) {
      tl.vars.onReverseComplete();
      tl.reverse();
    }
    if (config.draggable && typeof(Draggable) === "function") {
      let proxy = document.createElement("div"),
          wrap = gsap.utils.wrap(0, 1),
          ratio, startProgress, draggable, dragSnap, roundFactor,
          align = () => tl.progress(wrap(startProgress + (draggable.startX - draggable.x) * ratio)),
          syncIndex = () => tl.updateIndex();
      typeof(InertiaPlugin) === "undefined" && console.warn("InertiaPlugin required for momentum-based scrolling and snapping. https://greensock.com/club");
      draggable = Draggable.create(proxy, {
        trigger: items[0].parentNode,
        type: "x",
        onPress() {
          startProgress = tl.progress();
          tl.progress(0);
          populateWidths();
          totalWidth = getTotalWidth();
          ratio = 1 / totalWidth;
          dragSnap = totalWidth / items.length;
          roundFactor = Math.pow(10, ((dragSnap + "").split(".")[1] || "").length);
          tl.progress(startProgress);
        },
        onDrag: align,
        onThrowUpdate: align,
        inertia: true,
        snap: value => {
          let n = Math.round(parseFloat(value) / dragSnap) * dragSnap * roundFactor;
          return (n - n % 1) / roundFactor;
        },
        onRelease: syncIndex,
        onThrowComplete: () => gsap.set(proxy, {x: 0}) && syncIndex()
      })[0];
    }
    
      return tl;
  }
  });
  </script>

				</div>
					</div>
		</div>
					</div>
		</section>

				<div class="elementor-element elementor-element-3c220676 elementor-widget elementor-widget-theme-post-title elementor-page-title elementor-widget-heading" data-id="3c220676" data-element_type="widget" data-widget_type="theme-post-title.default">
					<h1 class="elementor-heading-title elementor-size-default">Clipper Malware disguised as AvD Crypto Stealer</h1>				</div>
				<div class="elementor-element elementor-element-1fcc1d6c elementor-widget elementor-widget-theme-post-excerpt" data-id="1fcc1d6c" data-element_type="widget" data-widget_type="theme-post-excerpt.default">
					Cyble Research Labs analyzes a Clipper malware variant disguised as an AvD Crypto-stealer, potentially targeting other Threat Actors.				</div>
				<div class="elementor-element elementor-element-2907e1e2 blog_content elementor-widget elementor-widget-theme-post-content" data-id="2907e1e2" data-element_type="widget" data-widget_type="theme-post-content.default">
					
<p>Information stealing malware is on the rise. Cyble Research Labs recently discovered a new malware dubbed “AvD crypto stealer” on a cybercrime forum. Upon further investigation, however, we observed that this does not function as a Crypto Stealer. This is, in fact, a disguised variant of well-known Clipper <a class="wpil_keyword_link" href="https://cyble.com/knowledge-hub/what-is-malware/" title="malware" data-wpil-keyword-link="linked" data-wpil-monitor-id="390" target="_blank">malware</a> that can read and edit any text copied by the victim i.e. crypto wallet information.</p>



<p>The TA is providing one month of free access to entice more individuals to use it. Anyone can become a victim of this malware – though the primary target appears to be other TAs.</p>



<p>The <a href="/blog/exposed-rdp-actively-targeted-by-threat-actors-to-deploy-ransomware/" title="Exposed Remote Desktop Protocol actively targeted by Threat Actors to deploy Ransomware" target="_blank" rel="noopener"  data-wpil-monitor-id="12970">Threat Actor</a> (TA) claims that the stealer supports six cryptocurrency chains, including Ethereum, Binance Smart Chain, Fantom, Polygon, Avalanche, and Arbitrum.</p><!-- This site is converting visitors into subscribers and customers with OptinMonster - https://optinmonster.com :: Campaign Title: Request demo blog -->
<div id="om-wlravxmwms40sunr2q0v-holder"></div>
<script>(function(d,u,ac){var s=d.createElement('script');s.type='text/javascript';s.src='https://a.omappapi.com/app/js/api.min.js';s.async=true;s.dataset.user=u;s.dataset.campaign=ac;d.getElementsByTagName('head')[0].appendChild(s);})(document,239265,'wlravxmwms40sunr2q0v');</script>
<!-- / OptinMonster -->



<p>The TA targets victims by changing the crypto addresses present in the clipboard. As for crypto transactions, individuals typically copy the crypto addresses, and the malware takes advantage of this by replacing the copied crypto wallet address with the one specified by TA.</p>



<p>If the victim does not validate the copied and the pasted values, then the transaction might end up in the account specified by TA. This <a href="/blog/multiple-new-clipper-malware-variants-discovered-in-the-wild/" title="Multiple New Clipper Malware Variants Discovered in the Wild" target="_blank" rel="noopener"  data-wpil-monitor-id="12968">clipper malware</a> can also identify the crypto addresses present amongst multiple strings, expanding this malware’s capabilities.</p>



<figure class="wp-block-image aligncenter size-large"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" width="1024" height="330" data-attachment-id="10153" data-permalink="https://cyble.com/blog/hunters-become-the-hunted/figure-1-post-shared-on-cybercrime-forum/" <h2 class="wp-block-heading" id="h-technical-analysis"><strong>Technical Analysis</strong></h2>



<p>The execution of malware starts from an installation file, which is Self-Extracting. Self-extracting archives, also known as SFX files, are Windows executable files that, upon execution, extract the compressed content. Figure 2 showcases the installation wizard.</p><div class="cyble-content_6" id="cyble-188813836"><div style="position: relative; padding-bottom: 15%; height: 0; overflow: hidden; max-width: 100%; height: auto;">

<figure class="wp-block-image aligncenter size-full"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" width="710" height="500" data-attachment-id="10154" data-permalink="https://cyble.com/blog/hunters-become-the-hunted/figure-2-installation-wizard/" data-orig-file="https://cyble.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/03/Figure-2-Installation-Wizard.png" data-orig-size="710,500" data-comments-opened="0" data-image-meta="{&quot;aperture&quot;:&quot;0&quot;,&quot;credit&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;camera&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;caption&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;created_timestamp&quot;:&quot;0&quot;,&quot;copyright&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;focal_length&quot;:&quot;0&quot;,&quot;iso&quot;:&quot;0&quot;,&quot;shutter_speed&quot;:&quot;0&quot;,&quot;title&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;orientation&quot;:&quot;0&quot;}" data-image-title="Figure-2-Installation-Wizard" data-image-description="" data-image-caption="" data-medium-file="https://cyble.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/03/Figure-2-Installation-Wizard-300x211.png" data-large-file="https://cyble.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/03/Figure-2-Installation-Wizard.png" src="https://cyble.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/03/Figure-2-Installation-Wizard.png" alt="" class="wp-image-10154" title="Clipper Malware disguised as AvD Crypto Stealer 12" srcset="https://cyble.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/03/Figure-2-Installation-Wizard.png 710w, https://cyble.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/03/Figure-2-Installation-Wizard-600x423.png 600w, https://cyble.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/03/Figure-2-Installation-Wizard-300x211.png 300w" sizes="(max-width: 710px) 100vw, 710px" /><figcaption class="wp-element-caption">Figure 2: Installation Wizard</figcaption></figure>



<p>The installation file drops the files shown in Figure 3 and executes the payload named <em>‘Payload.exe.’</em> The dropped files also contain manuals for using the builder and the binaries.</p>



<figure class="wp-block-image aligncenter size-full"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" width="639" height="212" data-attachment-id="10155" data-permalink="https://cyble.com/blog/hunters-become-the-hunted/figure-3-extracted-files/" data-orig-file="https://cyble.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/03/Figure-3-Extracted-files.png" data-orig-size="639,212" data-comments-opened="0" data-image-meta="{&quot;aperture&quot;:&quot;0&quot;,&quot;credit&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;camera&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;caption&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;created_timestamp&quot;:&quot;0&quot;,&quot;copyright&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;focal_length&quot;:&quot;0&quot;,&quot;iso&quot;:&quot;0&quot;,&quot;shutter_speed&quot;:&quot;0&quot;,&quot;title&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;orientation&quot;:&quot;0&quot;}" data-image-title="Figure-3-Extracted-files" data-image-description="" data-image-caption="" data-medium-file="https://cyble.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/03/Figure-3-Extracted-files-300x100.png" data-large-file="https://cyble.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/03/Figure-3-Extracted-files.png" src="https://cyble.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/03/Figure-3-Extracted-files.png" alt="" class="wp-image-10155" title="Clipper Malware disguised as AvD Crypto Stealer 13" srcset="https://cyble.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/03/Figure-3-Extracted-files.png 639w, https://cyble.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/03/Figure-3-Extracted-files-600x199.png 600w, https://cyble.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/03/Figure-3-Extracted-files-300x100.png 300w" sizes="(max-width: 639px) 100vw, 639px" /><figcaption class="wp-element-caption">Figure 3: Extracted files</figcaption></figure>



<p>The payload file (<strong>SHA256</strong>:<em>b6135c446093a19544dbb36018adb7139aa810a3f3eaa45663dc54448fe30e39</em>) is a .NET based binary. Figure 4 shows the payload details.</p>



<figure class="wp-block-image aligncenter size-full"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" width="714" height="425" data-attachment-id="10157" data-permalink="https://cyble.com/blog/hunters-become-the-hunted/figure-4-file-information/" data-orig-file="https://cyble.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/03/Figure-4-File-information.png" data-orig-size="714,425" data-comments-opened="0" data-image-meta="{&quot;aperture&quot;:&quot;0&quot;,&quot;credit&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;camera&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;caption&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;created_timestamp&quot;:&quot;0&quot;,&quot;copyright&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;focal_length&quot;:&quot;0&quot;,&quot;iso&quot;:&quot;0&quot;,&quot;shutter_speed&quot;:&quot;0&quot;,&quot;title&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;orientation&quot;:&quot;0&quot;}" data-image-title="Figure-4-File-information" data-image-description="" data-image-caption="" data-medium-file="https://cyble.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/03/Figure-4-File-information-300x179.png" data-large-file="https://cyble.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/03/Figure-4-File-information.png" src="https://cyble.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/03/Figure-4-File-information.png" alt="" class="wp-image-10157" title="Clipper Malware disguised as AvD Crypto Stealer 14" srcset="https://cyble.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/03/Figure-4-File-information.png 714w, https://cyble.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/03/Figure-4-File-information-600x357.png 600w, https://cyble.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/03/Figure-4-File-information-300x179.png 300w" sizes="(max-width: 714px) 100vw, 714px" /><figcaption class="wp-element-caption">Figure 4: File information</figcaption></figure>



<p>Figure 5 shows the process flow for the clipper malware. The malware extracts the data from the clipboard and then uses a regular expression to find the crypto addresses. If there’s a match, the malware replaces the address with one specified by TA.</p>



<figure class="wp-block-image aligncenter size-full"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" width="413" height="579" data-attachment-id="10158" data-permalink="https://cyble.com/blog/hunters-become-the-hunted/figure-5-clipper-malware-process-flow/" data-orig-file="https://cyble.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/03/Figure-5-Clipper-malware-process-flow.png" data-orig-size="413,579" data-comments-opened="0" data-image-meta="{&quot;aperture&quot;:&quot;0&quot;,&quot;credit&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;camera&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;caption&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;created_timestamp&quot;:&quot;0&quot;,&quot;copyright&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;focal_length&quot;:&quot;0&quot;,&quot;iso&quot;:&quot;0&quot;,&quot;shutter_speed&quot;:&quot;0&quot;,&quot;title&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;orientation&quot;:&quot;0&quot;}" data-image-title="Figure-5-Clipper-malware-process-flow" data-image-description="" data-image-caption="" data-medium-file="https://cyble.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/03/Figure-5-Clipper-malware-process-flow-214x300.png" data-large-file="https://cyble.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/03/Figure-5-Clipper-malware-process-flow.png" src="https://cyble.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/03/Figure-5-Clipper-malware-process-flow.png" alt="" class="wp-image-10158" title="Clipper Malware disguised as AvD Crypto Stealer 15" srcset="https://cyble.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/03/Figure-5-Clipper-malware-process-flow.png 413w, https://cyble.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/03/Figure-5-Clipper-malware-process-flow-214x300.png 214w" sizes="(max-width: 413px) 100vw, 413px" /><figcaption class="wp-element-caption">Figure 5: Clipper malware process flow</figcaption></figure>



<h3 class="wp-block-heading"><strong>Clipper malware has the following class names:</strong></h3>



<h4 class="wp-block-heading"><strong>Program:</strong></h4>



<p>This class contains the main function which executes the clipper functionalities. Upon execution, the main program creates a random mutex named “<em>XWj1iK27ngY68XUB</em>” to ensure that only one instance of the malware process runs at any given time. If it fails to create a mutex, the malware terminates its execution.</p>



<figure class="wp-block-image aligncenter size-full"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" width="802" height="275" data-attachment-id="10159" data-permalink="https://cyble.com/blog/hunters-become-the-hunted/figure-6-main-function/" data-orig-file="https://cyble.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/03/Figure-6-Main-function.png" data-orig-size="802,275" data-comments-opened="0" data-image-meta="{&quot;aperture&quot;:&quot;0&quot;,&quot;credit&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;camera&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;caption&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;created_timestamp&quot;:&quot;0&quot;,&quot;copyright&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;focal_length&quot;:&quot;0&quot;,&quot;iso&quot;:&quot;0&quot;,&quot;shutter_speed&quot;:&quot;0&quot;,&quot;title&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;orientation&quot;:&quot;0&quot;}" data-image-title="Figure-6-Main-function" data-image-description="" data-image-caption="" data-medium-file="https://cyble.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/03/Figure-6-Main-function-300x103.png" data-large-file="https://cyble.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/03/Figure-6-Main-function.png" src="https://cyble.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/03/Figure-6-Main-function.png" alt="" class="wp-image-10159" title="Clipper Malware disguised as AvD Crypto Stealer 16" srcset="https://cyble.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/03/Figure-6-Main-function.png 802w, https://cyble.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/03/Figure-6-Main-function-600x206.png 600w, https://cyble.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/03/Figure-6-Main-function-300x103.png 300w, https://cyble.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/03/Figure-6-Main-function-768x263.png 768w" sizes="(max-width: 802px) 100vw, 802px" /><figcaption class="wp-element-caption">Figure 6: Main function</figcaption></figure>



<p>After creating the mutex, the malware copies itself into the startup location to establish its persistence and executes <em>ClipboardNotification.NotificationForm() </em>function. Through this, the malware monitors the user’s clipboard activity, identifies crypto address, and replaces it with the attacker’s address details.&nbsp;</p>



<h4 class="wp-block-heading" id="h-clipboard-notification"><strong>Clipboard Notification:</strong></h4>



<p>&nbsp;This class monitors the user’s clipboard activity and notify when the user copies something into the clipboard.</p>



<h4 class="wp-block-heading" id="h-addresses"><strong>Addresses:</strong></h4>



<p>This class contains the config details, including crypto addresses, mutex name, and the <a href="/blog/new-enchant-android-malware-targeting-chinese-cryptocurrency-users/" title="New Enchant Android Malware Targeting Chinese Cryptocurrency Users" target="_blank" rel="noopener"  data-wpil-monitor-id="12972">targeted cryptocurrencies</a>, as shown in Figure 7. The clipper targets Bitcoin (BTC), Ethereum, and Monero (XMR) crypto addresses.</p>



<figure class="wp-block-image aligncenter size-full"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" width="936" height="394" data-attachment-id="10160" data-permalink="https://cyble.com/blog/hunters-become-the-hunted/figure-7-addresses-class/" data-orig-file="https://cyble.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/03/Figure-7-Addresses-class.png" data-orig-size="936,394" data-comments-opened="0" data-image-meta="{&quot;aperture&quot;:&quot;0&quot;,&quot;credit&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;camera&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;caption&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;created_timestamp&quot;:&quot;0&quot;,&quot;copyright&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;focal_length&quot;:&quot;0&quot;,&quot;iso&quot;:&quot;0&quot;,&quot;shutter_speed&quot;:&quot;0&quot;,&quot;title&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;orientation&quot;:&quot;0&quot;}" data-image-title="Figure-7-Addresses-class" data-image-description="" data-image-caption="" data-medium-file="https://cyble.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/03/Figure-7-Addresses-class-300x126.png" data-large-file="https://cyble.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/03/Figure-7-Addresses-class.png" src="https://cyble.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/03/Figure-7-Addresses-class.png" alt="" class="wp-image-10160" title="Clipper Malware disguised as AvD Crypto Stealer 17" srcset="https://cyble.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/03/Figure-7-Addresses-class.png 936w, https://cyble.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/03/Figure-7-Addresses-class-600x253.png 600w, https://cyble.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/03/Figure-7-Addresses-class-300x126.png 300w, https://cyble.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/03/Figure-7-Addresses-class-768x323.png 768w" sizes="(max-width: 936px) 100vw, 936px" /><figcaption class="wp-element-caption">Figure 7: Addresses class</figcaption></figure>



<h4 class="wp-block-heading" id="h-clipboard"><strong>Clipboard:</strong></h4>



<p>The class contains two function names, <em>GetText</em>() and <em>SetText</em>().</p>



<p>These functions get the clipboard text from the user. If there is a crypto wallet in the copied text, these functions will then set it to the attacker’s wallet address by replacing the copied user’s wallet address. Clipboard is also responsible for sending the data for logging purposes to the URL present in the Addresses class.</p>



<figure class="wp-block-image aligncenter size-full"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" width="739" height="460" data-attachment-id="10161" data-permalink="https://cyble.com/blog/hunters-become-the-hunted/figure-8-clipboard-class/" data-orig-file="https://cyble.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/03/Figure-8-Clipboard-class.png" data-orig-size="739,460" data-comments-opened="0" data-image-meta="{&quot;aperture&quot;:&quot;0&quot;,&quot;credit&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;camera&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;caption&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;created_timestamp&quot;:&quot;0&quot;,&quot;copyright&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;focal_length&quot;:&quot;0&quot;,&quot;iso&quot;:&quot;0&quot;,&quot;shutter_speed&quot;:&quot;0&quot;,&quot;title&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;orientation&quot;:&quot;0&quot;}" data-image-title="Figure-8-Clipboard-class" data-image-description="" data-image-caption="" data-medium-file="https://cyble.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/03/Figure-8-Clipboard-class-300x187.png" data-large-file="https://cyble.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/03/Figure-8-Clipboard-class.png" src="https://cyble.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/03/Figure-8-Clipboard-class.png" alt="" class="wp-image-10161" title="Clipper Malware disguised as AvD Crypto Stealer 18" srcset="https://cyble.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/03/Figure-8-Clipboard-class.png 739w, https://cyble.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/03/Figure-8-Clipboard-class-600x373.png 600w, https://cyble.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/03/Figure-8-Clipboard-class-300x187.png 300w" sizes="(max-width: 739px) 100vw, 739px" /><figcaption class="wp-element-caption">Figure 8: Clipboard class</figcaption></figure>



<h4 class="wp-block-heading"><strong>PatternRegex:</strong></h4>



<p>This class contains the regex pattern to identify the crypto addresses copied to the clipboard.</p>



<figure class="wp-block-image aligncenter size-full"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" width="624" height="221" data-attachment-id="10162" data-permalink="https://cyble.com/blog/hunters-become-the-hunted/figure-9-pattern-regex/" data-orig-file="https://cyble.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/03/Figure-9-Pattern-Regex.png" data-orig-size="624,221" data-comments-opened="0" data-image-meta="{&quot;aperture&quot;:&quot;0&quot;,&quot;credit&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;camera&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;caption&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;created_timestamp&quot;:&quot;0&quot;,&quot;copyright&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;focal_length&quot;:&quot;0&quot;,&quot;iso&quot;:&quot;0&quot;,&quot;shutter_speed&quot;:&quot;0&quot;,&quot;title&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;orientation&quot;:&quot;0&quot;}" data-image-title="Figure-9-Pattern-Regex" data-image-description="" data-image-caption="" data-medium-file="https://cyble.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/03/Figure-9-Pattern-Regex-300x106.png" data-large-file="https://cyble.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/03/Figure-9-Pattern-Regex.png" src="https://cyble.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/03/Figure-9-Pattern-Regex.png" alt="" class="wp-image-10162" title="Clipper Malware disguised as AvD Crypto Stealer 19" srcset="https://cyble.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/03/Figure-9-Pattern-Regex.png 624w, https://cyble.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/03/Figure-9-Pattern-Regex-600x213.png 600w, https://cyble.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/03/Figure-9-Pattern-Regex-300x106.png 300w" sizes="(max-width: 624px) 100vw, 624px" /><figcaption class="wp-element-caption">Figure 9: Pattern Regex</figcaption></figure>



<p>On further investigation into one of the hardcoded crypto addresses in the payload, we found the following transaction details, as shown below.</p>



<figure class="wp-block-image aligncenter size-full"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" width="936" height="415" data-attachment-id="10163" data-permalink="https://cyble.com/blog/hunters-become-the-hunted/figure-10-transaction-details/" data-orig-file="https://cyble.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/03/Figure-10-Transaction-details.png" data-orig-size="936,415" data-comments-opened="0" data-image-meta="{&quot;aperture&quot;:&quot;0&quot;,&quot;credit&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;camera&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;caption&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;created_timestamp&quot;:&quot;0&quot;,&quot;copyright&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;focal_length&quot;:&quot;0&quot;,&quot;iso&quot;:&quot;0&quot;,&quot;shutter_speed&quot;:&quot;0&quot;,&quot;title&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;orientation&quot;:&quot;0&quot;}" data-image-title="Figure-10-Transaction-details" data-image-description="" data-image-caption="" data-medium-file="https://cyble.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/03/Figure-10-Transaction-details-300x133.png" data-large-file="https://cyble.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/03/Figure-10-Transaction-details.png" src="https://cyble.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/03/Figure-10-Transaction-details.png" alt="" class="wp-image-10163" title="Clipper Malware disguised as AvD Crypto Stealer 20" srcset="https://cyble.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/03/Figure-10-Transaction-details.png 936w, https://cyble.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/03/Figure-10-Transaction-details-600x266.png 600w, https://cyble.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/03/Figure-10-Transaction-details-300x133.png 300w, https://cyble.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/03/Figure-10-Transaction-details-768x341.png 768w" sizes="(max-width: 936px) 100vw, 936px" /><figcaption class="wp-element-caption">Figure 10: Transaction details</figcaption></figure>



<p></p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading" id="h-conclusion"><strong>Conclusion:</strong></h2>



<p><a class="wpil_keyword_link" href="https://cyble.com/knowledge-hub/cyber-threat-actor-and-types/" title="Threat Actors" data-wpil-keyword-link="linked" data-wpil-monitor-id="881" target="_blank">Threat Actors</a> continue to exploit the human element for executing their attacks, as they see it as a vulnerability &#8211; this malware works on a similar attack vector. However, we can reduce the impact of this malware by being more cautious while making crypto transactions.</p>



<p>There are multiple possibilities in which this attack can escalate. In one of the scenarios, the malware creator can target other TA’s who use the builder for customizing the crypto stealer and their victims. This clipper can do financial theft at a great level, so it becomes necessary to take preventive measures.</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading" id="h-our-recommendations"><strong>Our Recommendations:&nbsp;</strong></h2>



<ul class="wp-block-list">
<li>Avoid downloading pirated software from warez/torrent websites. The “Hack Tool” present on sites such as YouTube, torrent sites, etc., primarily contains such malware. </li>



<li>Use a reputed anti-virus and <a href="/blog/the-rise-of-amadey-bot-a-growing-concern-for-internet-security/" title="The Rise of Amadey Bot: A Growing Concern for Internet Security" target="_blank" rel="noopener"  data-wpil-monitor-id="12974">internet security</a> software package on your connected devices, including PC, laptop, and mobile. </li>



<li>Refrain from opening untrusted links and email attachments without first verifying their authenticity.  </li>



<li>In the case of businesses, educate employees in terms of protecting themselves from threats like phishing’s/untrusted URLs. </li>



<li>Monitor the beacon on the network level to block data exfiltration by malware or TAs. </li>
</ul>

<script>
   let autoHideTimeout;

document.addEventListener('scroll', function() {
    var scrollPosition = window.scrollY || document.documentElement.scrollTop;
    var documentHeight = document.documentElement.scrollHeight - document.documentElement.clientHeight;

    // Calculate scroll percentage
    var scrollPercentage = (scrollPosition / documentHeight) * 100;

    // Check if the screen width is greater than 768px (for non-mobile devices)
    if (window.innerWidth > 768) {
        // Only activate the slider when scroll is between 60% and 100%
        if (scrollPercentage >= 60 && scrollPercentage <= 100) {
            // Show the slider by sliding it in
            document.getElementById('rightSlider').classList.add('active');

            // Clear any previous auto-hide timer
            clearTimeout(autoHideTimeout);

            // Set a 5-second timer to auto-slide the slider back out
            autoHideTimeout = setTimeout(function() {
                document.getElementById('rightSlider').classList.remove('active');
            }, 5000); // 5000 milliseconds = 5 seconds
        } else {
            // If not within 60% - 100% range, hide the slider
            document.getElementById('rightSlider').classList.remove('active');
        }
    }
});

document.getElementById('rightSlider').addEventListener('mouseover', function() {
    // On mouseover, keep the slider active and clear the auto-hide timer
    clearTimeout(autoHideTimeout);
    this.classList.add('active');
});

document.getElementById('rightSlider').addEventListener('mouseleave', function() {
    // On mouse leave, start the auto-hide timer again for 5 seconds
    clearTimeout(autoHideTimeout);
    autoHideTimeout = setTimeout(function() {
        document.getElementById('rightSlider').classList.remove('active');
    }, 5000); // 5000 milliseconds = 5 seconds
});

</script>				</div>

				(function() {
					// Global page view and session tracking for UAEL Modal Popup feature
					try {
						// Session tracking: increment if this is a new session
						
						// Check if any popup on this page uses current page tracking
						var hasCurrentPageTracking = false;
						var currentPagePopups = [];
						// Check all modal popups on this page for current page tracking
						if (typeof jQuery !== 'undefined') {
							jQuery('.uael-modal-parent-wrapper').each(function() {
								var scope = jQuery(this).data('page-views-scope');
								var enabled = jQuery(this).data('page-views-enabled');
								var popupId = jQuery(this).attr('id').replace('-overlay', '');	
								if (enabled === 'yes' && scope === 'current') {
									hasCurrentPageTracking = true;
									currentPagePopups.push(popupId);
								}
							});
						}
						// Global tracking: ALWAYS increment if ANY popup on the site uses global tracking
												// Current page tracking: increment per-page counters
						if (hasCurrentPageTracking && currentPagePopups.length > 0) {
							var currentUrl = window.location.href;
							var urlKey = 'uael_page_views_' + btoa(currentUrl).replace(/[^a-zA-Z0-9]/g, '').substring(0, 50);
							var currentPageViews = parseInt(localStorage.getItem(urlKey) || '0');
							currentPageViews++;
							localStorage.setItem(urlKey, currentPageViews.toString());
							// Store URL mapping for each popup
							for (var i = 0; i < currentPagePopups.length; i++) {
								var popupUrlKey = 'uael_popup_' + currentPagePopups[i] + '_url_key';
								localStorage.setItem(popupUrlKey, urlKey);
							}
						}
					} catch (e) {
						// Silently fail if localStorage is not available
					}
				})();
				</script>

				const lazyloadRunObserver = () => {
					const lazyloadBackgrounds = document.querySelectorAll( `.e-con.e-parent:not(.e-lazyloaded)` );
					const lazyloadBackgroundObserver = new IntersectionObserver( ( entries ) => {
						entries.forEach( ( entry ) => {
							if ( entry.isIntersecting ) {
								let lazyloadBackground = entry.target;
								if( lazyloadBackground ) {
									lazyloadBackground.classList.add( 'e-lazyloaded' );
								}
								lazyloadBackgroundObserver.unobserve( entry.target );
							}
						});
					}, { rootMargin: '200px 0px 200px 0px' } );
					lazyloadBackgrounds.forEach( ( lazyloadBackground ) => {
						lazyloadBackgroundObserver.observe( lazyloadBackground );
					} );
				};
				const events = [
					'DOMContentLoaded',
					'elementor/lazyload/observe',
				];
				events.forEach( ( event ) => {
					document.addEventListener( event, lazyloadRunObserver );
				} );
